  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fc87a4ae-cd13-4aa4-a47d-e003d37c4977'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/55343660-colorles"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/55343660-colorles">Colorles</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I absolutely adored this book, and I believe that if you are into a bit of fantasy and sci fi, you're bound to also! Evie was such a lovable main char<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I absolutely adored this book, and I believe that if you are into a bit of fantasy and sci fi, you're bound to also! Evie was such a lovable main character with a fun sense of humor. There's some really intense stuff in here, some nice feel-good stuff, a bit of romance(With a love triangle that I, being a person who's sick of love triangles, loved. I mean, come on, when one of the boys in the triangle is an insane faerie, how can you not love it?), some mystery.... I mean, this book is just all over the chart. It just has a way of drawing you in. Anyways, I'm ranting now, I would definitely recommend it!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2332940024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12183243812311683792"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605371177i/30377107._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Need a good read for a bad day? Here's a <u><b><a href='https://youtu.be/-GuEMAaGS3I' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booktube Video</a> </b></u> all about it!!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><br/><br/>I love, <i>love, <b> love, </b></i> this book. <br/><br/>I've read it on and off for the last ten years and every time I pick it up, <b>I literally<i> (yes, literally) </i>laugh out loud.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>Tasers are a one-size-fits-all paranormal butt-kicking option. Mine’s pink with rhinestones.</i>
</blockquote> I adore the premise, the subtle (and not-so-subtle) humor scattered throughout and the heroine is easily one of my YA faves. <br/><br/>Evie sees through glamors.<b> No </b></span>
  <span id="freeText12183243812311683792" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605371177i/30377107._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Need a good read for a bad day? Here's a <u><b><a href="https://youtu.be/-GuEMAaGS3I" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktube Video</a> </b></u> all about it!!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><br><br>I love, <i>love, <b> love, </b></i> this book. <br><br>I've read it on and off for the last ten years and every time I pick it up, <b>I literally<i> (yes, literally) </i>laugh out loud.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>Tasers are a one-size-fits-all paranormal butt-kicking option. Mine’s pink with rhinestones.</i>
</blockquote> I adore the premise, the subtle (and not-so-subtle) humor scattered throughout and the heroine is easily one of my YA faves. <br><br>Evie sees through glamors.<b> No one can hide from her. </b> From when she was discovered (at three) to now, she's been under the thumb of ICPA (Internatuonal Paranormal Containment Agency) as their <b>bagger-and-tagger. </b><br><br><b>Her job is pretty simple </b>- see a paranormal, neuter it (via tracking device) and bring it back to headquarters. BUT She isn't your average government employee/YA heroine. <br><br>When she's not rounding up the wild paranormals, she's<b> watching Easten Heights</b> (her absolute fave drama), <b>online shopping</b> (though most of the purchases get canceled by the government) and<b> hanging out with her best friend</b> (a mermaid).<br><br>When a <b>suspicious paranormal</b> shows up in the midst of a crisis Evie will have to figure out A) What's killing off the paranormals, B) How to stop her creepy ex-boyfriend (a faerie) from stalking her and C) If the suspicious-slash-hot new guy has a girlfriend.<i>
  <b> Not necessarily in that order.</b>
</i><blockquote>
  <i>He reached out and put his hand on top of mine. My heart skipped a beat - he liked me, too!<br><br>"You're worried about what's killing the paranormals aren't you?"<br><br>Crap. He didn't like me.</i>
</blockquote> The sincerity, the sass. Gah. I want Evie to be my best friend. If you're looking for a refreshing take on YA fiction - pick it up! <blockquote>
  <i>“What are you?" I whispered.<br><br>"What are you?" <br><br>Offended, I frowned. "Human."<br><br>"Funny, me too."<br><br>"No, you're not."<br><br>"Funny, neither are you."</i>
</blockquote><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Emily Eiden and she absolutely rocked this audio. She had the right tempo/timing for the humor - really made Evie come alive.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_112471231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112471231" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112471231?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the YA Paranormal genre</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=should-have-been-bad">should-have-been-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=ya-pnr-maddness">ya-pnr-maddness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112471231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10942086507702597653">There’s a scene in Vampire’s Suck (yes, my husband and saw it with a group of friends and exited the cinema a few hours later with a few less braincells). Vampire’s Suck’s version of Mike Newton from Twilight approached the Bella character upon meeting her, threw an arm around her shoulder and said, “Wow, you look pretty frigid and boring! Wanna go to prom?”<br/><br/>Despite the stupidity of this movie they managed to encapsulate, in one brilliant sentence, the biggest problem I’ve had with the YA paranor</span>
  <span id="freeText10942086507702597653" style="display:none">There’s a scene in Vampire’s Suck (yes, my husband and saw it with a group of friends and exited the cinema a few hours later with a few less braincells). Vampire’s Suck’s version of Mike Newton from Twilight approached the Bella character upon meeting her, threw an arm around her shoulder and said, “Wow, you look pretty frigid and boring! Wanna go to prom?”<br><br>Despite the stupidity of this movie they managed to encapsulate, in one brilliant sentence, the biggest problem I’ve had with the YA paranormal novels of late. Particularly Fallen, Hugh Hush, Evermore, Halo, and the countless others like it that I haven’t managed to torture myself with. The female main characters are BORING. What’s more, they’re written in the roles of heroines and tragically couldn’t act less heroic. <br> <br>Unless those bitches were hiding their sheballs somewhere I couldn’t see. (Yes, most women totally have sheballs.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337424i/695065.jpg" alt="Chrisella" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Except for Chris Crocker…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337424i/695066.jpg" alt="sheballs!!!!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>See?<br><br>Evie is such a refreshing departure. She’s funny and, here’s something new, FUN. From her crazy antics and funny obsessions to even the most simple of phrases that come from her mouth. <br><br>Now, I’ll briefly explain about the Mary Sue test. Most authors and people in general are familiar with this term. It basically means the Main Character, if she is a Mary Sue, is basically an author self-insert. <br><br>Otherwise known as Luce, Nora, Ever, Bethany, Clary, Tessa and the biggest Mary Sue ever – Anita Blake.<br><br>Though imagining yourself doing various and weird sexual acts with Jean “I stole my leather pants from a hooker and now she wants them back” Claude is just a little weird.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337424i/695067.jpg" alt="Tranny Pants!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately Evie ticks quite a few boxes on the Mary Sue test:<br><br>Evie is remarkably beautiful.<br><br>Evie carries an unusual weapon, wears a strange piece of jewelry, or otherwise displays a unique possession on her person.<br><br>Evie is notably witty, always ready with a sharp comeback or clever remark. Alternatively, she is fascinatingly stern and close-mouthed.<br><br>She is a natty dresser, always in fashion, or not in fashion but so well as to make the fashionable pale in comparison.<br><br>There's an unusual story centering around Evie's birth or infancy.<br><br>She was adopted, raised by people other than her parents, or for some reason has no biological parents.<br><br>There are prophecies about Evie.<br><br>Evie has psychic abilities, exceptional strength, magical powers, can heal with a touch, or has any other skill, talent, or power that we would consider superhuman.<br><br>	More Than one special power.<br><br>	Practically no one else in the story has similar powers.<br><br>But you know, she never feels like a Mary Sue. I guess her cute yearning for cars, high school, lockers, television and all the other little quirks to her personality give her a rounded character.<br><br>I thoroughly enjoyed the relationship between Evie and Lend. Not only did they have some witty and fun banter. There’s also that rare feeling that I have when I read novels, that these two could actually make it. I’m serious in that I could actually see these two getting married and the whole happily ever after too. They really make a lovely couple.<br>Unlike some people…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337424i/695068.jpg" alt="Anita and Jean Claude twu loff!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anita and Jean Claude know how to have a good time together… no really!<br><br>The plot and pacing move nicely throughout the story and whilst it was easy to guess who the bad guy was and what the eventual outcome would be, it didn’t annoy me like it has in other novels. Can I help it if I’m, like, practically a genius or something? <br>No, no I can’t!<br><br>So over all this novel was a breath of fresh air. I completely enjoyed it and I absolutely can’t wait to read the sequel! I highly recommend it to most people, except for anyone named Bob and I think that out of most of the other YA paranormal lit out there, this one is definitely the best.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10942086507702597653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130380204" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130380204" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130380204?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA urban fantasy readers, Buffy fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      SCB TBR 2011 - Pick Three; Jess
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=tbr-scb-2011">tbr-scb-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130380204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6502398606425863209">When you look at the cover of this book, what do you think it is about? A blond teenage girl is wearing a prom dress in a field of pussy willows or wheat or something equally nonsensical. Here's a new cover that crushes the actual book cover on the relevancy front (though regrettably not in terms of artistic merit):<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341346i/697519._SY540_.jpg' width='406' height='428' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I mean, I went into this thinking it was going to be another YA paranormal romance and IT ISN'T. It is decidedly fun YA <b>urban fantasy</b> book. (jacket copy reading is for losers) It has </span>
  <span id="freeText6502398606425863209" style="display:none">When you look at the cover of this book, what do you think it is about? A blond teenage girl is wearing a prom dress in a field of pussy willows or wheat or something equally nonsensical. Here's a new cover that crushes the actual book cover on the relevancy front (though regrettably not in terms of artistic merit):<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341346i/697519._SY540_.jpg" width="406" height="428" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, I went into this thinking it was going to be another YA paranormal romance and IT ISN'T. It is decidedly fun YA <b>urban fantasy</b> book. (jacket copy reading is for losers) It has a pretty kickass heroine, mermaids, werewolves (that may or MAY look like an Ewok in my picture), people made of water, people made of fire, vampires, trolls, nymphs, faeries, and everything else you can think of. Why would you trick your audience with the wheat field? <br><br>I digress. Evie has lived in the Center for as long as she can remember. She was picked up at the age of three and put through the foster system until the IPCA (Int'l Paranormal Containment Agency) realizes that she can see through glamours produced by all paranormals. As a vital asset, she goes out to bag-and-tag all sorts of beings for the agency. Things get a little dicey when all sorts of paranormals are being killed, the Center is invaded, and some faeries are being total douchebags. Speaking of faeries, Reth sounds like a noise someone makes when they are choking on something. Reeeth...Reeeeth...I'm retching here, it's too bad you can't hear it. <br><br>I felt like the last third or so wasn't as strong as the rest of the book. The story moved at a relaxed but appealing pace until a total break occurred and then it was out of whack. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The moment Evie looks, sees a sign for the prom, and then Lend asks her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Fun, sure, but I was perfectly happy with the natural pacing of the relationship--I was glad it wasn't going into trite YA foreverlove territory, and it still didn't...but it did get a little cheesified.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Kiersten%20White" title="Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiersten White</a> has a great sense of humor. Her characters were funny and fans of Buffy will definitely find something appealing about the friendships and storyline. I'm excited to see where it goes in the second book--<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152887673" rel="nofollow noopener">Supernaturally</a>.(which, incidentally, has Evie in a red dress and with some red (and probably completely irrelevant) flowers on the cover) <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm a little bit annoyed that Evie left Vivian alive/potentially alive. Just kill the villain already! And naming your taser "Tasey"...blech. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> 3.5 stars.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_166635663" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166635663" />
    <a title="Haleema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema"><img alt="Haleema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402430795p2/4336293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166635663?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haleema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haleema" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema">Haleema</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166635663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11986759516211969500">I do not have the patience to read a book where the heroine talks like this:<br/><br/>"Oh bleep! I'm so pumped! He kissed me! It was the best kiss of my life! It's such a cool kiss!" <br/><br/>Oh bleep?<br/><br/><i>Oh bleep?</i><br/><br/>I'm out. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_165475074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165475074" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165475074?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165475074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14003804009655196606"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>(Young adult genre + supernatural creatures) x love triangle - originality = De ja bloody vu</b><br/><br/>Why even bother reading this book? I can point you towards hundreds of other young adult books that are more or less exactly the same as what you get from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7719245-paranormalcy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paranormalcy</a>. I keep going back to this kind of genre, hoping that just once I will find the exception to the current book cloning rule that seems to be taking over the 21st century. We have a heroine who is neither good or bad enough to be exciting</span>
  <span id="freeText14003804009655196606" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>(Young adult genre + supernatural creatures) x love triangle - originality = De ja bloody vu</b><br><br>Why even bother reading this book? I can point you towards hundreds of other young adult books that are more or less exactly the same as what you get from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7719245-paranormalcy" rel="nofollow noopener">Paranormalcy</a>. I keep going back to this kind of genre, hoping that just once I will find the exception to the current book cloning rule that seems to be taking over the 21st century. We have a heroine who is neither good or bad enough to be exciting, she's not exactly weak but doesn't have much strength to note, and the attempts to give her some kind of quirky sense of humour failed. She has a taser gun (my first thought: "cool!"), which she has named "Tasey" (not so cool). I thought the only people who named their guns were cops caught in a mid-life crisis. Apparently not.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349326i/703347.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Why do I get the feeling that I've met every single one of these characters before? Oh, that's right... because I have. So, yeah, they have different names but that's about it. Also, what exactly is the big story here? Some sort of unheard of supernatural creature is killing other supernatural creatures by leaving a big fiery handprint on them. Well, that's genius. It wasn't even a <i>good</i> unoriginal story. And naturally there's a love triangle going on too. It seems that most young adult authors don't know how not to put a love triangle in their books. This time it's Lend v. Reth. Lend is quite a cute character and my favourite of the pair; mostly because, wait for this, Reth repeatedly attempted some kind of supernatural rape thing - not good at all. No really, I don't know what it was all about but he kept trying to "fill her" with his "warm essence". Wtf?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349326i/703348.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book started to really drag about half way through and I kept pushing myself to finish it because I'm sick of abandoning books, an abandoned book feels like a fail on my part. So I braved it til the end, even though I did do a bit of skimming on the last few chapters. My conclusion? Well, I can sort of, maybe, possibly see why some people might like this. It's not completely awful, but I do wish I'd stuck with my initial instincts when I saw the quote by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2876763.Becca_Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Becca Fitzpatrick</a> on the front cover and thought "uh-oh".<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349326i/703349.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14003804009655196606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97737063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97737063" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3471319-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512402337p2/3471319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97737063?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/3471319-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=paid-full-price">paid-full-price</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97737063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11641722337101378484">I probably would've given a slightly higher star rating if there hadn't been so much damn hype around this book.<br/><br/>Alright. I'm feeling pro/con-y today. I'm taking a break from pharmacology homework to write this, so I need to get back to that. And it's a football Saturday, I've got a Bud Light in hand, so my thoughts are less than structured.<br/><br/>Pros:<br/>- The cover is pretty, even though I can't decide how it correlates to the story. <br/>- There is a seriously wide variety of paranormal creatures in this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText11641722337101378484" style="display:none">I probably would've given a slightly higher star rating if there hadn't been so much damn hype around this book.<br /><br />Alright. I'm feeling pro/con-y today. I'm taking a break from pharmacology homework to write this, so I need to get back to that. And it's a football Saturday, I've got a Bud Light in hand, so my thoughts are less than structured.<br /><br />Pros:<br />- The cover is pretty, even though I can't decide how it correlates to the story. <br />- There is a seriously wide variety of paranormal creatures in this book, each type having their own special powers/abilities. Vamps, werewolves, fey, water nymphs, mermaids, hags, gnomes, trolls. Yay for a smorgasbord of weirdness! <br />- The idea behind the book is cool. The International Paranormal Containment Agency hires Evie to track down unruly paranormals who threaten the unveiling of their existence, allowing her to tase them to the fullest extent of her desire.<br />- Evie is an especially special (heh) abnormal human who can see through paranormal creatures' glamours. She kicks serious butt and can take down a gaggle of vamps without a second thought. <br />- I didn't lose interest in the book throughout the first 4/5 of the novel. <br />- Evie's fascination with lockers was cute and funny.<br />- There were some really clever lines in this book. The interaction between Lend and Evie caused some near-LOLs.<br /><br />Cons:<br />- Evie was annoying. I found her cute at first. Ya know, she's a girl who doesn't get out much (read: ever) and she clings to whatever sense of normalcy available with every fiber of her being. She watches hip teen shows and wears zebra print dresses and pink stiletto boots. She has a right to be a little weird. But somewhere along the line, she just began to grind my gears and wasn't cute anymore. I can't get much more descriptive than that, really, because I don't know when exactly she began to annoy me.<br />- Lackluster love interests. Reth was semi-appealing at first, until he uttered the line "let me fill you." I think I temporarily lost control of my gag reflex and gastric content at that moment. I later found out it didn't mean what I thought it meant, but WHO CARES?! That line should never be used in any context whatsoever, unless he's a bartender offering to fill her drink or a millionaire offering to fill her bank account. Lend just bored me. He shouldn't have bored me because he's your typical nice guy who isn't quite normal and, like the heroine, is looking for somewhere to belong. But he just didn't do it for me. <br />- Pink taser with rhinestones? Acceptable. Pink taser with rhinestones named "Tasey?" *facepalm* *headdesk* *keysmash* OAIm PA7A *Wrj H~! LK#(*&amp;%(T~~!!!!<br />- The villain wasn't scary.<br />- The weird, hokey ending with the floating and the souls and the WTF.<br /><br /><br />This book may appeal to many people and apparently has. I'll probably read the sequel, but I'm not rushing out to get it. If you like cutesy books with happy little rainbow endings, by all means, help yourself. It could've been better, though.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11641722337101378484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1619585570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1619585570" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1619585570?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1619585570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6249626241228912574"><blockquote>
  <i>Being dead wasn't supposed to hurt. Where was the fairness in that? If I was dead, the least the universe could do was make it painless.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This novel was actually <b>awfully</b> written but the plot was funny, and so was the main character. I mean, I'm sure Kiersten's writing has improved and the only reason I picked this one up is because I wanted to see how her writing is/was. I'm sure the other 2 books are much better and now that <i>And I Darken</i> is almost published, I'm sure that one will have much m</span>
  <span id="freeText6249626241228912574" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Being dead wasn't supposed to hurt. Where was the fairness in that? If I was dead, the least the universe could do was make it painless.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This novel was actually <b>awfully</b> written but the plot was funny, and so was the main character. I mean, I'm sure Kiersten's writing has improved and the only reason I picked this one up is because I wanted to see how her writing is/was. I'm sure the other 2 books are much better and now that <i>And I Darken</i> is almost published, I'm sure that one will have much more improvements. I wanted to see how her writing is and what changes might be made. <br /><br />The writing in this one is pretty bad. I mean, the main character, Evie, is <b>pretty annoying, not much of a heroine, pretty weak, and instead of cussing, she says "bleep" because she's so used to hearing it from her best friend who is a mermaid.</b> Other than that, she's pretty <b>confident with herself and her jokes are bad but they made me laugh.</b> <i>(Because they were bad</i>) <br /><br />This isn't really a typical YA romance-paranormal novel that deals with vampires, faeries, mermaids, werewolves and other paranormals. It dealt with romance but it wasn't a main point. It mainly focused on finding out who was killing all these paranormals and what/who is Evie. Because she can see through the glamours of a paranormal, she is considered not only human but a paranormal herself. See, if there is a vampire with their glowing bright yellow eyes walking in the streets of Miami, FL, someone will think "Ooh pretty eyes, nice color" and they won't know that creature is a bloody-sucking creature, but Evie immediately knows. She sees yellow eyes behind the brown ones, blue ones behind the grey ones, and she sees what kind of paranormal it is. But there comes the mysterious one, Lend, who is introduced as some shape-shifter who turns out to become Evie's friend and I guess <i>boyfriend?</i> Sadly, there was a love-triangle. It wasn't a big one and it wasn't much of a distraction, but it still bugged me.<br /><br />Love triangles are something I do not like. I think they are useless and pointless and they ruin the story most of the time. <i>We always get introduced to the main female and male character but then some other male character is introduced and well, that's where the love triangles is sensed. The main female character leaves the main male character and falls for the other male character.</i> Wow that was confusing even for me.<br /><br />The reason the love triangle wasn't a big distraction was because it wasn't really a love triangle. What I mean is, Evie falls for Lend and spends time with him while her ex, Reth (a faerie) tries to <i>win her heart back, touch her, make her his</i> and blah blah blah all that. But, Evie doesn't really want him back. Sure she misses <i>his arms wrapped around her and her thin waist, his warmth around her, his protection over her</i> and everything else they did. But after she saw who he really was and what he did to her (which is around page 100 and on) she doesn't want anything to do with him. I was okay with that! I shipped her with Lend (sort of) and didn't want her going back to Reth. The only reason why I sense a love triangle was because I thought she would go back to Reth, since she was talking to Lend and becoming his friend while she was thinking about Reth.<br /><br />The plot was hard to get at first. I didn't understand it. I didn't know what the book was really about, where it was going, and what was the point of it. It did take a while, and because of the lack of writing and stupid horrible jokes, nothing really made sense at one point. It was hard to get into it and there were times where I put the book down because it was a really frustrating and stupid part, I didn't want to continue reading. Hopefully the 2nd and 3rd books are better!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6249626241228912574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160215421" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160215421" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160215421?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-liked-it">i-liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable">it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=vamps">vamps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=original-and-creative">original-and-creative</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160215421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7000383008467379801"><br/>Actual rating 2.5 stars. <br/><br/>Let me start by saying that I didn't hate this book, but I also didn't love it either. It was cute, spunky, and funny. However, there was just something about it that annoyed me. <br/><br/>So I've recently found out what a Mary Sue is. All this time I've been calling it "A la Bella-esque." Evie is most defiantly a Mary Sue. And I've come to the realization that I had a love/hate relationship with Evie the entire book. I thought she was really funny and down right silly at times. B</span>
  <span id="freeText7000383008467379801" style="display:none"><br />Actual rating 2.5 stars. <br /><br />Let me start by saying that I didn't hate this book, but I also didn't love it either. It was cute, spunky, and funny. However, there was just something about it that annoyed me. <br /><br />So I've recently found out what a Mary Sue is. All this time I've been calling it "A la Bella-esque." Evie is most defiantly a Mary Sue. And I've come to the realization that I had a love/hate relationship with Evie the entire book. I thought she was really funny and down right silly at times. BUT at the same time she annoyed me with being so cheerful with her love of all things pink. I kept flipping back an forth. Sometimes I felt her endearing. Yet other times I wanted to bitch slap her. <br /><br />But I digress. I did find a few things I liked about the book. I found Evie's relationship with Lend to be very realistic. It wasn't over done. They weren't ripping their clothes off after only dating for a week. They weren't confessing their undying love for one another. Actually, I would say the romance kinda took a backseat in this book. It was there, but it didn't feel like it controlled the plot. Also, I did find the book really funny. Awesome dialog. Bonus points for no cliffhanger. <br /><br />Anyway, I can't really think of anything else to add to this review right now. It just didn't leave a lasting impression like I had hoped. I will continue with the series. More so, out of curiosity for where the story will go. <br /><br />More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>

<div id="review_122436635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122436635" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2098381-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474068564p2/2098381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122436635?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2098381-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122436635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1242699694780395799">I'll admit it, I was lured into reading this one due to the oh so lovely cover as I'm a huge sucker for pink. Luckily, Evie, the narrator of Paranormacly, shares my enthusiasm for the rosy hue. However, that's about all we share aside from our love of shopping.<br/><br/>I'm contemplating joining a YA paranormal support group. More often than not, these reads fail to deliver. I need to cut the ties that bind and admit this genre is no longer what it once was. Or perhaps I've matured as a reader. But seeing</span>
  <span id="freeText1242699694780395799" style="display:none">I'll admit it, I was lured into reading this one due to the oh so lovely cover as I'm a huge sucker for pink. Luckily, Evie, the narrator of Paranormacly, shares my enthusiasm for the rosy hue. However, that's about all we share aside from our love of shopping.<br /><br />I'm contemplating joining a YA paranormal support group. More often than not, these reads fail to deliver. I need to cut the ties that bind and admit this genre is no longer what it once was. Or perhaps I've matured as a reader. But seeing as I bought this book for the pretty pink cover, I rather doubt it. Nevertheless, the books within this YA paranormal genre are no longer up to par. I wanted to relish in this one, hoping against hope that it would be as funny as the blurbs boasted. I had myself convinced that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7719245.Paranormalcy__Paranormalcy___1_" title="Paranormalcy (Paranormalcy, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Paranormalcy</a> would be similar to Buffy the Vampire Slayer with a bit of Georgia Nicholson thrown in for good measure. Alas, thou hast been deceived once again by duplicitous marketing genius. <br /><br />I should have known that if several authors I have no respect for thought this was “The sexiest, scaries and funniest new addition to the paranormal genre” that I need to turn tail and run. This book is about as sexy and "scary" as "The Little Mermaid, and let's face it, "The Little Mermaid" was much more humorous. In fact, "The Little Mermaid" was a bit more menacing when I think about it. The sea witch had me going for a minute there, and at one point I was terrified that she would marry Prince Eric and Ariel would be trapped forever as a mute without her fishy friends to keep her company, but I digress. <br /><br />As I mentioned, this book lacked humor, I didn't laugh once, not even an internal chuckle. Evie simply isn't intelligent enough to be witty, nor is she ridiculous enough to laugh at. I'm a bit confused as to what exactly I was meant to find humorous. Worse, there wasn't a single moment of swoon. Did I mention that I used to have a raging crush on Prince Eric? I used to dream I could be turned into a mermaid with a singing voice, just so I could become mute in order to be made back into the human I am. Oh the glories of being 5 years old! See what I did right there? I compared the maturity level of this 17 year old narrator to my 5 year old self, *sigh*. Speaking of sighs, brace yourself, because this book is chalk full of them. People are sighing all thie time up in this tome. Now I know what you're thinking, you can't believe that a book lacking in maturity or humor couldn't at least boast of having a hottie. Well, let me tell you, don't believe the dust jacket. The dust jacket claims that there are two guys vying for Evie's affection, insinuating a sordid love triangle that those of us with wavering reading morals live for. Sadly Evie hates one of these mentioned studs, with good reason I might add, and the other is just so ordinary and innocent that I hardly had to catch the drool. There simply wasn't any angst, anywhere. <br /><br />Read for brain candy if you must, but I for one, recommend you waste your hard earned dollars on something a bit more entertaining, like "The Little Mermaid".<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1242699694780395799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_134502317" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134502317" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134502317?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people looking for a less angsty, more fun YA paranormal</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=g-ya-paranorm">g-ya-paranorm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134502317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17388195907229153169">First off, I really liked Evie. She reminded me of Mac (from the Fever series) a little, and that can't be a bad thing. I'm usually very fastidious when it comes to finding heroines that I like, but Evie was actually really nice.<br/>She may have had a couple of blonde moments towards the end (no offense to blondes, of course - my mother is actually blonde) but I still think she was fierce, fun, refreshing, and insecure in a way that I found quite endearing. I alternated between wanting to grab her a</span>
  <span id="freeText17388195907229153169" style="display:none">First off, I really liked Evie. She reminded me of Mac (from the Fever series) a little, and that can't be a bad thing. I'm usually very fastidious when it comes to finding heroines that I like, but Evie was actually really nice.<br />She may have had a couple of blonde moments towards the end (no offense to blondes, of course - my mother is actually blonde) but I still think she was fierce, fun, refreshing, and insecure in a way that I found quite endearing. I alternated between wanting to grab her and hug her and wanting to go shopping with her. She just has that aura about her. And when the time came for her to make the right decision, she made it. Plain and simple. There was no messing everything up so that the stage is set for the next book to have a bunch of obstacles to move and things to fix that could have easily been avoided if the heroine had only made the right decision. To be blunt, she wasn't stupid (like some heroines I won't mention here *cough*Ever*cough*).<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although there was one thing that she could've done differently: I wanted her to kill—or at least find some thorough way to get ride of—her sister. <i>That</i> particular story line did irk me a little. I know that seems harsh, but nothing good can come from her sister IMO. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Lend was completely different from what I was expecting. Kind, sweet, yet protective when the situation called for it. He was the perfect yang to Evie's yin.<br />And the paranormal aspect with him seemed more unique than most out there right now; I liked that.<br /><br />I've never been a big fan of faeries when they're the kind that manipulate and take you away from where you're clearly supposed to be. So I think it's safe to say that I didn't really like Reth. But, in this case, I'm not quite sure you're supposed to. It seems to me that the author wants us to know he's not really a second choice for Evie—unless he changes drastically in the next installment—so much as an obstacle for Evie to overcome. So, as far as love triangles go, I'd say this novel doesn't really have one (YES! That's a good thing, IMO). And here's to hoping that doesn't change in the next installment.<br /><br />Now, I think the only thing I haven't mentioned is the writing. I think that some may read this novel and feel that it's maybe too cutesy or fluffy; however, for me, it was just a nice change of pace from all of the angsty YA romances that seem to be so popular. <br /><br />So, <i>Paranormalcy</i> is a good debut and I look forward to seeing where this story goes in the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8581936.Supernaturally__Paranormalcy___2_" title="Supernaturally (Paranormalcy, #2) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Supernaturally</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17388195907229153169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8517503118409431507">I wrote a longer review of <i>Paranormalcy</i> back in 2010. At the time, I had just started my book-review blog, and this was one of the first ARCs I ever received. So I think there was a lot to originally endear me to the story, and it was definitely light, cute, and a quick read.<br/><br/>But then I tried to read the sequel, and I subsequently discovered that "light" and "cute" books just didn't hold my interest anymore. The characters (Evie? her mermaid friend?) were a bit too "ABC Family" for my taste (i.e.</span>
  <span id="freeText8517503118409431507" style="display:none">I wrote a longer review of <i>Paranormalcy</i> back in 2010. At the time, I had just started my book-review blog, and this was one of the first ARCs I ever received. So I think there was a lot to originally endear me to the story, and it was definitely light, cute, and a quick read.<br /><br />But then I tried to read the sequel, and I subsequently discovered that "light" and "cute" books just didn't hold my interest anymore. The characters (Evie? her mermaid friend?) were a bit too "ABC Family" for my taste (i.e. trying for interesting/perhaps even provocative, but only succeeding in being over-the-top and slap-worthy). <br /><br />So in retrospect, I have to remove <i>Paranormalcy</i> from my 'Favorites' shelf. It's a good book, I'd definitely recommend it to younger readers or 'chick lit meets lite fantasy' fans, but...I guess I've outgrown books like this. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68958519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7169487468109280208">This novel had me hooked from the first page. I mean with an intro like this how can you not want to read the rest:<br/><br/>“Wait- did you-- You just yawned!” The vampire’s arms , raised over his head in the classic Dracula pose, dropped to his sides. He pulled his exaggerated white fangs back behind his lips. “What, imminent death isn’t exciting enough for you?”<br/><br/>“Oh, stope pouting. But, really, the widow’s peak? The pale skin? The black cape? Where did you even get that thing, a costume store?” <br/><br/>If that d</span>
  <span id="freeText7169487468109280208" style="display:none">This novel had me hooked from the first page. I mean with an intro like this how can you not want to read the rest:<br /><br />“Wait- did you-- You just yawned!” The vampire’s arms , raised over his head in the classic Dracula pose, dropped to his sides. He pulled his exaggerated white fangs back behind his lips. “What, imminent death isn’t exciting enough for you?”<br /><br />“Oh, stope pouting. But, really, the widow’s peak? The pale skin? The black cape? Where did you even get that thing, a costume store?” <br /><br />If that doesn’t have you stifling a laugh and anxious for more.... well you must have an incredibly boring sense of humor.. or you might be dead! <br /><br />I think for a book described as a paranormal, I was expecting something a little more serious... and perhaps dark. But I should have known from those first lines that this book was going to be different! I think that’s why I liked it so much, it is definitely different.<br /><br />Evie was such a great character. She’s innocent and completely ignorant... but it works. It’s the life that she’s lived, she’s always been sheltered and left in the dark. I think that made her character memorable. At least for me, I know it did. Evie stood out. <br /><br />The prophecy thing.... which I don’t really want to say much about, really took me for a loop. I was totally engrossed in what was going on with the agency and trying to figure out who the bad guy was, the prophecy sort of snuck up on me! The added mystery surrounding that, really added to the suspense of the novel! <br /><br />A paranormal that is funny, engrossing and memorable.... it can only mean one thing.... AWESOME! <br /><br />I can not wait to dig into book two and see what Kiersten has up her sleeve! <br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2507910-peep-pop-pop?shelf=addicted-to-ya">addicted-to-ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120769850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3075193649453033836">Yeahhhhh, so this one started out pretty funny. I kind of liked Evie. Though I did think she was much less mature than what you think someone would be, based on her level of confinement. <br/><br/>The bad guy was ok. I didn't really see her as intimidating. I mean, she really wasn't. Her wrath was kind of peaceful. I thought what they did to paranormals was wrong,</span>
  <span id="freeText3075193649453033836" style="display:none">Yeahhhhh, so this one started out pretty funny. I kind of liked Evie. Though I did think she was much less mature than what you think someone would be, based on her level of confinement. <br /><br />The bad guy was ok. I didn't really see her as intimidating. I mean, she really wasn't. Her wrath was kind of peaceful. It's hard to explain but I felt like they were just rumors of a bad guy, that there was no actual bad guy in this book.<br /><br />I did not like the IPCA. I thought what they did to paranormals was wrong, wrong, wrong. It was slavery, slavery I tell you!<br /><br />I was all set to complain about the lack of answers in this book. No explanation of what paranormalcy is, nothing about how that stun gun worked. You mean to tell me not one single PN was immune to a measly stun gun?? How the heck can you be paranormal then? I'd call you different, but not paranormal! <br /><br />I think this was the first book that I've read where the paranormals were extremely lame and so unimpressive. They were weaker than humans. They let humans control them. How could you not know basic self defense? I mean, they let themselves get caught by a 16 year old girl with a stun gun who admittedly does not work out!!! Do they have bricks for feet or something?? Really, they sit and patiently take accept it and politely ask questions. Me? I'd ask a question to distract her, karate chop her in the neck, and run like there's a 49 cent sale on best sellers at the nearest bookstore. <br /><br />I think most people would still like this one. It was funny in most places and extremely clean. There was no excessive violence and no bad language. It was lighthearted but just not enough to get more stars from me. The ending was kind of lame and anti-climatic. <br /><br />I liked Lend, Lissa and David. There was someone else I liked but I couldn't read the name I wrote in my notes (and I already returned the book)! I still don't know about Reth.<br /><br />And the cover lies! It is a beautiful cover, but it was all lies. The cover makes you think it's dark, but it's not. It's light and campy (not a bad thing, but the cover lies!)</span>

<div id="review_148239371" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148239371" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148239371?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148239371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7136986734894970207">This is the book that you read when you need a break from dark, serious, hefty novels and just want something fun! Paranormalcy not simply about vampires, or werewolves, or faeries, it's includes ALL of them- and more. I really had a great time with it and enjoyed the medley.<br/><br/>Evie can see paranormals: No matter what glamour they wear, she can see through it. She's been living with the IPCA, an agency who controls the paranormals, all her life and feels pretty lonely being the only (human) teenage</span>
  <span id="freeText7136986734894970207" style="display:none">This is the book that you read when you need a break from dark, serious, hefty novels and just want something fun! Paranormalcy not simply about vampires, or werewolves, or faeries, it's includes ALL of them- and more. I really had a great time with it and enjoyed the medley.<br /><br />Evie can see paranormals: No matter what glamour they wear, she can see through it. She's been living with the IPCA, an agency who controls the paranormals, all her life and feels pretty lonely being the only (human) teenager there. Evie is an incredibly fun character. She has wit, spunk and a definite sense of humor. I loved how she gets excited for the smallest things - like lockers - and we get to see her take in the real world. I also didn't get an annoyed teenager vibe from her. Evie is very mature for her age which I imagine comes from being raised by IPCA as well as seeing unimaginably icky things daily. However, it doesn't change the fact that she longs for a boyfriend like on her favourite show, and wishes she could just go to real high school prom.<br /><br />Evie soon meets a very intriguing love interest, Lend. He's like nothing she's ever seen before - literally. I loved Lend. He's the type of noble guy that you can always count on. His relationship with Evie is not instant either, it progresses at a great pace where you can see and feel their attraction grow. I was also delighted with the lack of a love triangle. I enjoy love triangles as much as the next, but sometimes it's nice to get a change of pace.<br /><br />As for the plot, it's just plain fun! Vampires, fairies, mermaids, werewolves, wookies, you name it. Don't expect anything too deep or elaborate, but do count on a lot of attitude, pink weapons and interesting twists! And all of this in a quick, satisfying read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7136986734894970207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115326380" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115326380" />
    <a title="Janina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3455554-janina"><img alt="Janina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404584313p2/3455554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115326380?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007390120" href="/book/show/8713858-paranormalcy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=given-away">given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115326380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17882428068123797862"><b>Paranormalcy</b> definitely was a cute little book. It was entertaining, funny and a little romantic at times – but, honestly, while I enjoyed it, it didn’t really make a lasting impression on me. <br/><br/>Evie was very pink, but also very refreshing when compared to other heroines I’ve met so far. I loved her little quirks and her excitement when it came to ‘normal’ life. Her obsession with her pink rhinestone taser ‘Tasey’ (something that had me <i>very</i> suspicious at the beginning) actually didn’t bother me t</span>
  <span id="freeText17882428068123797862" style="display:none"><b>Paranormalcy</b> definitely was a cute little book. It was entertaining, funny and a little romantic at times – but, honestly, while I enjoyed it, it didn’t really make a lasting impression on me. <br /><br />Evie was very pink, but also very refreshing when compared to other heroines I’ve met so far. I loved her little quirks and her excitement when it came to ‘normal’ life. Her obsession with her pink rhinestone taser ‘Tasey’ (something that had me <i>very</i> suspicious at the beginning) actually didn’t bother me that much. It was kind of cute. Lend was a great love interest, not particularly swoon worthy, but interesting and sweet nevertheless. Liked all the different kinds of paranormal creatures and their specialities. But overall, I just didn’t care <i>that</i> much for the characters and I also thought that the story lost a bit of its steam around the two third mark. I found the ‘final battle’ very anticlimactic. It was almost over before it really began. The ending left things opens for the sequel, but avoided a mean cliffhanger – thankfully. <br /><br />All in all, I liked it, but it just wasn’t that big a thing for me. <br />If I can swap the next instalment, I think I’ll give it a read. But I can’t say that I’m dying to get my hands on it, and with all the great books coming out all the time, I might forget about it until September …<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17882428068123797862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89201978" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89201978" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89201978?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007390120" href="/book/show/8713858-paranormalcy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=swapped-or-given-away">swapped-or-given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=mystery-crime-sleuthing">mystery-crime-sleuthing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=mermaids-underwater-breathers">mermaids-underwater-breathers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=faeries-elves-pixies">faeries-elves-pixies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=paranormal-humans">paranormal-humans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89201978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer942985233967218584">I was skeptical after I read a ton of reviews and saw that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2876763.Becca_Fitzpatrick' title='Becca Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Becca Fitzpatrick</a> recommended it (very bad sign in my opinion), but I decided not to cancel my pre-order and have a go. Now I have to say: I really liked the book. And I liked the heroine and her love-interest (I mention only one, because that manipulative control-freak behavior of RetCh, the conscience-free faerie, cannot be counted as love-triangle worthy. He just used her loneliness and her craving of any kind of physical contact to r</span>
  <span id="freeText942985233967218584" style="display:none">I was skeptical after I read a ton of reviews and saw that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2876763.Becca_Fitzpatrick" title="Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Becca Fitzpatrick</a> recommended it (very bad sign in my opinion), but I decided not to cancel my pre-order and have a go. Now I have to say: I really liked the book. And I liked the heroine and her love-interest (I mention only one, because that manipulative control-freak behavior of RetCh, the conscience-free faerie, cannot be counted as love-triangle worthy. He just used her loneliness and her craving of any kind of physical contact to reach his goal. There is really NOTHING to recommend or excuse him apart from good looks. So don't try to convince me of the opposite. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2096360.Aprilynne_Pike" title="Aprilynne Pike" rel="nofollow noopener">Aprilynne Pike</a> wrote in her blurb "...One won Evie's heart and the other won mine." I enjoyed Mrs. Pikes debut well enough to rate it three stars, but after this disclosure of her bad taste in evil guys I will be very wary of books to come).<br /><br />After reading her story I can even understand Evie's girlish preference for pink, sparkling clothes and tasers and her motivation to give her Taser and her knife pet names: Since she turned eight she has been living underground, held like a dumb princess in an ivory tower, fed with only the information necessary to tag and bag random paranormals for the International Paranormal Containment Agency that is her "home" and shamelessly uses her unique gift of seeing beyond every kind of magic glamour. All her confidants are grown-ups. She is home-schooled by a permanently depressed female werewolf and High-School is something that happens on TV. If you were Evie, would you not jump at every possibility to shop with your otherwise business-like guardian for some ultra-girlish clothes, which resemble the stuff the actors on your favorite Teen TV Drama "Easton Heights" flaunt? Would you not try to be a little normal, to be a teenager? Evie does not own rhine-stone-studded hand-bags because she never leaves the Center outside of a mission. So she compensates by decorating her weapon and giving it a silly name.<br /><br />Apart from the difference in age and that unhealthy degree of helpers syndrom Rachel Morgan has, Evie's personality reminded me a lot of this favorite urban fantasy heroine of mine. I don't excactly know why. But she was not at all how I had imagined her to be.<br /><br />What I also liked were the various commonly known paranormal lores (faerie, vampire, werewolf, mermaid, elementals ...), their adaption and their integration into the book's world-building. Nicely done. I think I will pickup the sequel "Supernaturally", when it comes out in paperback.</span>
  <a data-text-id="942985233967218584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8195482511715702063">This was <b>so much fun</b>!!! Considering how old this is and what a throwback it is to the 2010's-era of YA...I didn't think I would. I have no idea why I didn't read this back in middle school when I was reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5287473.Hex_Hall__Hex_Hall___1_' title='Hex Hall (Hex Hall, #1) by Rachel Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hex Hall</a> and every other YA paranormal book under the sun! Better late than never, I guess! :P<br/><br/>I think that the best part of the book is the protagonist, <b>Evie</b>, herself. She's just so fun and spunky and <i>enthusiastic</i> about everything we'd consider to be mundane and normal! She had the potential</span>
  <span id="freeText8195482511715702063" style="display:none">This was <b>so much fun</b>!!! Considering how old this is and what a throwback it is to the 2010's-era of YA...I didn't think I would. I have no idea why I didn't read this back in middle school when I was reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5287473.Hex_Hall__Hex_Hall___1_" title="Hex Hall (Hex Hall, #1) by Rachel Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Hex Hall</a> and every other YA paranormal book under the sun! Better late than never, I guess! :P<br /><br />I think that the best part of the book is the protagonist, <b>Evie</b>, herself. She's just so fun and spunky and <i>enthusiastic</i> about everything we'd consider to be mundane and normal! She had the potential of becoming a typical Mary Sue, but instead, was just an innately good person and <i>full of light</i>. I loved her! <br /><br />I also loved the world Kiersten White created. Usually paranormal books stick to no more than a few supernatural creatures, but this book was <i>FILLED</i> with them! From faeries to werewolves to vampires to mermaids to hags ... <i>SO MANY</i>!!! ...I'm also really curious as to what Evie truly is :o<br /><br />There's not much I didn't like (even though the use of "<b>bleep</b>" as a curse word was irritating, but eventually, I stopped noticing it), so I can't wait to continue the series! :D</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>,
